### PERILOUS RESEARCH


A Lasting Legacy
================



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/styles/auth_small/public/images/person/080214_1291.jpg)

Jacob Van Lunen

Jacob Van Lunen began playing Magic in 1995. He has participated in organized play at every level of competition and was a member of the winning team at Pro Tour San Diego in 2007, thanks to an innovative draft strategy. As a writer, Van Lunen has had more than three hundred Magic strategy pieces published


October 30, 2014
 










Welcome back to Perilous Research, DailyMTG.com's exclusive *Magic Online* column. Last weekend, 481 Legacy stalwarts showed up in Philadelphia to try their hand in the [Legacy Championship](http://magic.wizards.com/en/events/coverage/eternalweekend14). In the coming weeks, we'll continue to watch as the *Magic Online* Legacy metagame adapts to powerful delve cards from *Khans of Tarkir*. Today, we'll be discussing the delve cards' effect on the Legacy format and taking a look at the best-performing decks from last weekend's Legacy Championship!


With [Treasure Cruise](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Treasure+Cruise) and [Dig Through Time](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dig+Through+Time) in the format, Legacy has become a much different animal. So, how did Legacy change in response to *Khans of Tarkir*?




[![](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Treasure Cruise)](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Treasure Cruise)


[![](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Dig Through Time)](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dig Through Time)



First, mana creatures like [Noble Hierarch](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Noble+Hierarch) and [Deathrite Shaman](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deathrite+Shaman) went down in value by a significant margin. It's hard to play cards that interact unfavorably with [Forked Bolt](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Forked+Bolt) and [Lightning Bolt](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lightning+Bolt) in the new Legacy. Historically, these types of cards haven't been that bad for mana guys because, in the strictest of terms, it's just an opponent trading one card and one mana for one card and one mana. However, the one mana spent by the opponent has a lot of hidden value. The [Lightning Bolt](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lightning+Bolt) that's killing our [Deathrite Shaman](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deathrite+Shaman) might also be flipping a [Delver of Secrets](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Delver+of+Secrets), making a token with [Young Pyromancer](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Young+Pyromancer), or making [Treasure Cruise](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Treasure+Cruise) have a reduced casting cost. The hidden advantages add up quickly.


One for one discard spells become worse. Sure, they're still great cards against the combo strategies, but picking apart an opponent's hand only to see it get refilled by [Treasure Cruise](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Treasure+Cruise) is backbreaking. The decks that play [Treasure Cruise](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Treasure+Cruise) have very aggressive game plans and can punish our life total when we're using turns, cards, and mana to affect their hand and not the battlefield.


Next, [Tarmogoyf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tarmogoyf) gets worse. Opponents are exiling their graveyards, so [Tarmogoyf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tarmogoyf) now trades with [Lightning Bolt](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lightning+Bolt) a pretty decent portion of the time. Additionally, [Young Pyromancer](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Young+Pyromancer) makes in unfavorable to attack with a [Tarmogoyf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tarmogoyf) because it can just be chump-blocked indefinitely while the opponent swings back for significant amounts of damage. The decreased value of discard spells contributes significantly to [Tarmogoyf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tarmogoyf)'s downfall.




[![](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Tarmogoyf)](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tarmogoyf)


[![](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Lightning Bolt)](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lightning Bolt)



[Dig Through Time](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dig+Through+Time) gives miracles a legitimate card-advantage engine. In the past, the deck has relied on assembling [Counterbalance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Counterbalance)/[Sensei's Divining Top](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sensei%27s+Divining+Top) early in many matchups. Now, the deck gets to be more malleable, especially in post-boarded games, finding whatever tool it needs at a given time, allowing the deck to play a more pure-control game. The deck has also been historically bare minimum in terms of cards it can pitch to [Force of Will](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Force+of+Will), and a few copies of [Dig Through Time](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dig+Through+Time) do a lot to pad that hole in the game plan.


Protection from red is a very real ability in the new Legacy. [Kor Firewalker](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Kor+Firewalker) is one of the best cards against the Blue-Red Delver decks and we can probably expect a lot more of those, at least in the sideboards, in Death and Taxesâ€“style White Weenie decks.


Reanimator and decks that go big with cards like [Veteran Explorer](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Veteran+Explorer) are also much better than they've been in the past. Dropping [Griselbrand](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Griselbrand) into play on the second or third turn is nearly impossible for the Blue-Red Delver decks to beat.




[![](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Kor Firewalker)](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Kor Firewalker)


[![](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Griselbrand)](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Griselbrand)



The Blue-Red Delver strategies want to be aggressively trading one for one while attacking the opponent's life total with backup disruption. We can't play their game if we want to win. We need to weather the storm and win the game with cards that require two cards or more if we're going to stand a chance. Cards that get better in this regard include [Brimaz, King of Oreskos](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brimaz%2C+King+of+Oreskos); [True-Name Nemesis](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=True-Name+Nemesis); [Wurmcoil Engine](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wurmcoil+Engine); [Elesh Norn, Grand Cenobite](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Elesh+Norn%2C+Grand+Cenobite); and [Griselbrand](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Griselbrand).


With Grand Prix New Jersey right around the corner and various other high-profile Legacy events on the horizon, this seems like a great time to get involved with the format. What should we play? Here are the decklists of the top 32 finishers from the Legacy Championship.

![](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Force+of+Will)



















*Khans of Tarkir* has drastically changed the landscape of the Legacy format. Going forward, we'll need to build our decks in such a way that they're better suited to handle the delve cards. The cards have all been thrown into the air, and it's only a matter of time before we see where everything lands. In the coming weeks, we'll continue to explore various Constructed formats as we make our way toward the end of the year.


On a light note, *Commander* (2014 Edition) is fast approaching and preview season is in full swing. Like many others, my favorite card zone when playing Commander is the graveyard. I love stocking up the yard and making interesting and complicated plays to swing the tides of a game in the blink of an eye. Today's preview card is exciting in aggressive decks, graveyard-themed decks, and token strategies.


Let's check out Hallowed Spiritkeeper!


![](https://media.wizards.com/2014/c14/aakdfnppleih2/en_oavp4obwx7.png)
There's a lot of nuance to this guy, and he's very good no matter what angle you're coming from.


First, it's an exceptional midgame threat. We'll be able to repeatedly attack for 3 without repercussion in most situations because getting Hallowed Spiritkeeper off the table will mean that a fresh army of tokens will soon be on the way.


It forces opponents to combo a removal spell with their board sweepers if they want to actually clean up the entire battlefield.


If we're aggressively filling our graveyard with cards like [Commune with the Gods](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Commune+with+the+Gods), [Grisly Salvage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Grisly+Salvage), or dredge cards, we'll often be able to make north of twenty tokens when we sacrifice Hallowed Spiritkeeper.


There's an interesting push and pull going on with Hallowed Spiritkeeper where we want to make room for anthem effects like [Glorious Anthem](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Glorious+Anthem) or [Crusade](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Crusade), but we also need our deck to be mostly creatures. As a result, cards that double as both are especially strong alongside Hallowed Spiritkeeper. Look for creatures with [battle cry](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Search/Default.aspx?output=spoiler&method=visual&text=+[battle]+[cry]), [Celestial Crusader](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Celestial+Crusader), [Wilt-Leaf Liege](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wilt-Leaf+Liege), or other cards that pump the team while also contributing to our creature count.


There's a lot of power in Hallowed Spiritkeeper and the card does a good job of keeping non-Sultai graveyard decks afloat and reasonable. Sure, [Sidisi, Brood Tyrant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sidisi%2C+Brood+Tyrant) is a nice commander, but we can play a token/graveyard deck with cards like [Gavony Township](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gavony+Township) and it might be even more impressive.


Hallowed Spiritkeeper is sure to take over a lot of Commander games in the coming months.


Knowledge is power!
